  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_77fd5b02-4ed8-44d9-b3f8-93f792f8612f'
      });
    }

      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);

  <span id="freeText4519334117741965795" style="display:none">The action and adventure continue for Gregor in this stunning fantasy from Suzanne Collins, bestselling author of the Hunger Games. New cover art coming July 1st! <br />Gregor swears he will never return to the Underland, that strange world below New York City. But he is a key player in another prophecy, this one about an ominous white rat called the Bane. The Underlanders know there is only one way to lure Gregor back to their world: by kidnapping his little sister, Boots.<br />Now Gregor's quest reunites him with his bat, Ares, and the rebellious princess Luxa. They descend into the dangerous Waterway in search of the Bane. If Gregor does not fulfill the prophecy, his life, and the Underland, will never be the same.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer4686756922426834708"><i> "Allow me to translate," said Twitchtip, not even bothering to move. "She said if you don't stop your incessant babble, the big rat sitting in the boat next to you will rip your head off." </i><br/><br/>Wow. My emotions.<br/><br/>The first time I read this book, it was on audio because it was always checked out from my local library. And I distinctly remember lying on my bed, with my portable CD player next to me, listening to the end of this book with tears in my eyes. The impact this story had on me is crazy.<br/><br/>Some of</span>
  <span id="freeText4686756922426834708" style="display:none"><i> "Allow me to translate," said Twitchtip, not even bothering to move. "She said if you don't stop your incessant babble, the big rat sitting in the boat next to you will rip your head off." </i><br /><br />Wow. My emotions.<br /><br />The first time I read this book, it was on audio because it was always checked out from my local library. And I distinctly remember lying on my bed, with my portable CD player next to me, listening to the end of this book with tears in my eyes. The impact this story had on me is crazy.<br /><br />Some of my favorite characters in this whole series are introduced in this book. Howard is a good, soft boy and I would marry him in a minute, just thought y'all should know. Twitchtip is fantastically sassy and still gives me all the feels. Photos Glow-Glow and Zap are not my faves but to me now, they are hilarious whereas when I was a kid they annoyed me to no end. We also get more development for Ares and Luxa and Ripred and Temp. And good grief I just love these characters.<br /><br />This book is where it all gets real. A lot goes down, a lot changes. Gregor grows up a lot. And wow, it's done so well.<br /><br />5 stars, obviously.</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3078296195" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17623905121187672469">Okay, this is <i>much</i> more like it. I was a little lukewarm on <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/262430.Gregor_the_Overlander__Underland_Chronicles___1_' title='Gregor the Overlander (Underland Chronicles, #1) by Suzanne Collins' rel='nofollow noopener'>Gregor the Overlander</a>, but <i>Gregor and the Prophecy of Bane</i> is better imo. It's much darker and gorier, with real moral/ethical dilemmas, characters still wrestling with their grief from the previous book, some dire consequences that will have payoff in future book(s), and one of my favourite themes: former allies not being quite so understanding and good as they appear. I'm really starting to get the sense that this is the same author b</span>
  <span id="freeText17623905121187672469" style="display:none">Okay, this is <i>much</i> more like it. I was a little lukewarm on <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/262430.Gregor_the_Overlander__Underland_Chronicles___1_" title="Gregor the Overlander (Underland Chronicles, #1) by Suzanne Collins" rel="nofollow noopener">Gregor the Overlander</a>, but <i>Gregor and the Prophecy of Bane</i> is better imo. It's much darker and gorier, with real moral/ethical dilemmas, characters still wrestling with their grief from the previous book, some dire consequences that will have payoff in future book(s), and one of my favourite themes: former allies not being quite so understanding and good as they appear. I'm really starting to get the sense that this is the same author behind <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2767052.The_Hunger_Games__The_Hunger_Games___1_" title="The Hunger Games (The Hunger Games, #1) by Suzanne Collins" rel="nofollow noopener">The Hunger Games</a>, and I think the prose was a bit more sophisticated, too.<br /><br />Gregor and Ares' evolving dynamic is the greatest thing (A BONE-DEEP FRIENDSHIP FORGED THROUGH ADVERSITY!!), and I really like Gregor as a protagonist: he's well-intentioned and kind and not wanting to fit into the 'ruthless warrior' box that the Underlanders keep wanting to put him into. His nontraditional background still feels so fresh and important, too, as an impoverished family in the city, struggling to afford groceries. These books also continue to champion the message of not painting an entire people with the same brush. <br /><br />There's so many loose threads and conflict left to resolve that Gregor is now eager to return to the Underland, and so am I. :']<br /><br />Buddy-read with Stephanie!</span>

<div id="review_388286658" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/388286658" />
    <a title="Gerasimos Reads " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11731184-gerasimos-reads"><img alt="Gerasimos Reads " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1601542847p2/11731184.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/388286658?book_show_action=true">Aug 10, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Gerasimos Reads " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Gerasimos Reads " href="/user/show/11731184-gerasimos-reads">Gerasimos Reads </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback " href="/book/show/17795060-gregor-and-the-prophecy-of-bane">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11731184-gerasimos-reads?shelf=own">own</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer388286658" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5247285948338000829"><br/>Suzanne Collins is a masterful author. The Hunger Games trilogy is a masterpiece. One of my most favorite books. I do believe that in a few years it will become a classic. When I was done with the Hunger Games trilogy with the release of Mockingjay I was thirsty for more books by her. So I decided to try her first series, the Underland Chronicles. When I opened the pages of Gregor the Overlander last year, I admit it: I was affraid. Not because it is a book that appeals to children, since I love</span>
  <span id="freeText5247285948338000829" style="display:none"><br />Suzanne Collins is a masterful author. The Hunger Games trilogy is a masterpiece. One of my most favorite books. I do believe that in a few years it will become a classic. When I was done with the Hunger Games trilogy with the release of Mockingjay I was thirsty for more books by her. So I decided to try her first series, the Underland Chronicles. When I opened the pages of Gregor the Overlander last year, I admit it: I was affraid. Not because it is a book that appeals to children, since I love Middle Grade, but because I was scared that Collins would not meet my expectations. I proved to be wrong. Collins can write superb for both kids and adults. With this second book in the Underland Chronicles proves for once again what a great author she is. <br /><br />At first glance this series seems completely different from the Hunger Games. But it really isn't. Collins it both her series talks about war and its consequences. She describes violence and pain in an outstanding way. In this series, since it is for children she talks about war in a more smoother way than she does in the Hunger Games. But she is not affraid to describe violence, pain and death shockingly. Not only that but she also does not hesitate to kill her characters, even the most main ones. <br /><br /> Exactly like in the Hunger Games, Collins uses her characters and what happens to them as parallels to historical events and personalities. Younger audiences may not understand the parallels but an adult sees easily that the war between rats, bats and all the other mesmerizing creatures of the Underland is used in order to talk about Nazism and World War. The similarities with the Hunger Games however do not end there. Like in her other trilogy she uses ancient greek and roman empire references. <br /><br />The story in this book is more than enjoyable. Collins has created a world that dazzles the reader. Bats, rats, fireflies, spiders and people with violet eyes and pale skin live together in an Underland fantasy beautiful on the outside but dark and putrefied because of war on the inside. The characters are so lovable. Collins ability to create multidimensional characters whose actions surprise you is breathtaking. The action and twists are masterfully done. Every chapter leaves you craving for more. <br /><br />The story in this book is much more interesting than in the first one. First of all, the set, the sea part of the Underland, is really more entertaining. Collins introduces new places as she continues building her beautiful world. New characters are also introduced, and old ones are explored deeper. The adventures and the agony are much more present. The ending leaves you with a beautiful twist that makes you want to read the next book immediately. <br /><br />An amazing read for both kids and adults. It is the perfect read for younger audiences that cannot yet read the Hunger Games, but it also great for Collins' fans. Α mesmerising adventure that combines light with darkness, loss and grief with love and hapiness, heartwarming moments with action and humor with anguish. Suzanne Collins is one of the best authors in modern literature and reader should definitely have an eye on her works! </span>
  <a data-text-id="5247285948338000829" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText239304223533053277" style="display:none">THIS SERIES...so good. I have no words. <br /><br />Not going to write a long review for this one, but I loved all of it. Which makes me wish there was even more hype surrounding this series. I feel like Gregor has grown so much as a character in this book. <div id="review_1488387508" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1488387508" />
    <a title="Claudia {SparrowHawk}" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9133267-claudia-sparrowhawk"><img alt="Claudia {SparrowHawk}" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1602320728p2/9133267.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1488387508?book_show_action=true">Jan 01, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Claudia {SparrowHawk}" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Claudia {SparrowHawk}" href="/user/show/9133267-claudia-sparrowhawk">Claudia {SparrowHawk}</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9133267-claudia-sparrowhawk?shelf=adventure">adventure</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9133267-claudia-sparrowhawk?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9133267-claudia-sparrowhawk?shelf=family-friendly">family-friendly</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9133267-claudia-sparrowhawk?shelf=middle-grade">middle-grade</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9133267-claudia-sparrowhawk?shelf=childrens">childrens</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9133267-claudia-sparrowhawk?shelf=non-stop-action">non-stop-action</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9133267-claudia-sparrowhawk?shelf=perseverance-and-human-will">perseverance-and-human-will</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9133267-claudia-sparrowhawk?shelf=unexpected-plot-twist">unexpected-plot-twist</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9133267-claudia-sparrowhawk?shelf=male-protagonist">male-protagonist</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9133267-claudia-sparrowhawk?shelf=series">series</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1488387508" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10230980770143114650">
  <a href='http://www.mysoulcalledlife.com/category/sparrows-book-reviews/' rel='nofollow noopener'>
    <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1452144697i/17651720._SX540_.png' width='400' height='150' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
  </a>
<br/><br/><i>Gregor and the Prophecy of Bane</i> was an engaging read and served more as a gradual process of revelations to pave the way for the following three books in the series. It was long enough to adequately flesh out its characters and the atmosphere in the Underland – this along with the emphasized significance of the plot consistently impressed me – I liked it!<br/>___________________________________<br/><b>
  <u>WHAT I LIKED</u>
</b><br/>+ All of the familiar tropes from the middle-grade/fantasy genres are piled up i</span>
  <span id="freeText10230980770143114650" style="display:none">
  <a href="http://www.mysoulcalledlife.com/category/sparrows-book-reviews/" rel="nofollow noopener">
    <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1452144697i/17651720._SX540_.png" width="400" height="150" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
  </a>
<br><br><i>Gregor and the Prophecy of Bane</i> was an engaging read and served more as a gradual process of revelations to pave the way for the following three books in the series. It was long enough to adequately flesh out its characters and the atmosphere in the Underland – this along with the emphasized significance of the plot consistently impressed me – I liked it!<br>___________________________________<br><b>
  <u>WHAT I LIKED</u>
</b><br>+ All of the familiar tropes from the middle-grade/fantasy genres are piled up in this book, but are either altered or provided with emphasized significance, and (as with all Suzanne Collins books) offer a heavy dose of lessons on morality. That’s what I enjoy about Collins’ books, though ― how they naturally manage to tug at the strings of my heart and expose increasingly dark truths about my given nature. The plot ultimately turned out to be a refreshing lineup of familiar tropes and relatively fresh material.<br><br>+ The characters are rather common archetypes; however, I admired how their one-dimensional personalities flourished even more in this plot line than in book one. Too, I really enjoyed how their quest served as a testing of fire and how the circumstances leading up to the conclusion made them susceptible to their flaws and weaknesses – they faced tough decisions, they encountered even more powerful foes, they were forced to lay their differences aside and trust one another, they grew in friendship, and even laid down their lives! It goes without saying that the majority of character development takes place during the battles themselves; especially the ones that were life-threatening. It was all so tragically beautiful and impressive.<br><br>+ At the center of all the commotion in <i>Gregor and the Prophecy of Bane</i>, one character, in particular, stole my heart, and that is Twitchtip. Oh, how I loved this precious rat; I loved her snippy personality, her snide remarks and just the tragedy surrounding her back story – she was born with an invaluable gift and because of this, her very own kin cast her aside!<br><blockquote>All those years of living alone in the Dead Land had left her desperate to touch any warm being. Even him.</blockquote><br>+ The world and atmosphere in the Underland is both majestic and awesome-ly creepy. There are stunning nightmarish labyrinths and oceans that teem with twisted imagery, and legendary creatures. I also enjoyed how in the midst of all this sodden chaos, Suzanne Collins began to unveil the dark, oppressive and painful reality of the Underland world ― which in the end, in light of its clever cliffhanger, leaves you begging for more.<br><br><br><br><b>
  <u>THINGS THAT MADE GO HMMM. . .</u>
</b><br>- I have to admit, I wasn’t fully immersed in the story at first. I suspect it’s mainly because I read a lot from the YA and Adult Fiction genres; thus, I had to force myself to push through the chapters whilst, of course, bearing in mind that these books are geared towards a younger audience. I should mention that the story begins to pick up a quarter into the book!<br><br>- The Underland Chronicles has a huge array of characters – witty animal protagonists (rats, cockroaches, moths, fireflies, spiders, bats, you name it!), mythical creatures and beings, even an adorable two-year-old toddler who plays a somewhat pivotal role. I admit this large casts overwhelms at times and I sense I am not truly appreciating them all. <br><br>- How Suzanne Collins managed to create a world in the underground sewers of New York is beyond me. As brilliant as the idea may be, I confess that I found this world incredibly difficult to grasp. Firstly, I just couldn’t get a picture of brimming rivers overflowing into a vast ocean ― really? An ocean in an underground sewer? Second, just how big are these bats, rats, and critters? Granted, Suzanne Collins alludes to the topic, but only to a certain extent. Needless to say, I’m still trying to visualize an eleven-year-old confronting a nine-foot rat! Alas, I blame this on my black and white fashion.<br><br><br><br><br><b>
  <u>AFTERTHOUGHTS:</u>
</b><br>Here’s the summation, while ostensibly for children, I went into <i>Gregor and the Prophecy of Bane</i> expecting a fun mindless romp but in the end, I cried, cowered in a corner for fostering murder in my heart, and walked away with this message:<br><br>Biased thinking leads to hatred → hatred proceeds to action → action proceeds to murder; thus, the moral of this story?<br><blockquote>If he had killed it, he would have never been the same. He would have lost himself forever.</blockquote><br><br><a href="http://www.mysoulcalledlife.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> || <a href="https://www.facebook.com/thisismysoulcalledlife/timeline" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> || <a href="https://twitter.com/Sparrow_Hawk24" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> || <a href="https://plus.google.com/+ClaudiaArroyoMySoulCalledLife/posts" rel="nofollow noopener">Google+</a> || <a href="https://www.bloglovin.com/blogs/my-soul-called-life-13502715" rel="nofollow noopener">Bloglovin'</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="10230980770143114650" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <a title="Becky" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1978609-becky"><img alt="Becky" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1233429155p2/1978609.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/306024857?book_show_action=true">Apr 03, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Becky" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Becky" href="/user/show/1978609-becky">Becky</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781407121147" href="/book/show/11020186-gregor-and-the-prophecy-of-bane-suzanne-collins">review of another edition</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer306024857" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18298031898969995830">After staying up until 1 in the morning to finish book 1 I was eager to dig into book 2. I was at work today and had to go out in my lunch break, but luckily I finished early today so once I got home at 3.30 I got to sit down and get stuck in. By 5.00 I was over halfway through. This one is 50 pages longer than book 1, coming in at 308 pages, but that is still not a lot for me. <br/>I stopped for dinner then picked the book up again and was finished by 7.00. Once again I had powered through it, swept</span>
  <span id="freeText18298031898969995830" style="display:none">After staying up until 1 in the morning to finish book 1 I was eager to dig into book 2. I was at work today and had to go out in my lunch break, but luckily I finished early today so once I got home at 3.30 I got to sit down and get stuck in. By 5.00 I was over halfway through. This one is 50 pages longer than book 1, coming in at 308 pages, but that is still not a lot for me. <br />I stopped for dinner then picked the book up again and was finished by 7.00. Once again I had powered through it, swept into the pages and taken on a journey with Gregor. The evening seemed to flash past me.<br />Gregor thought getting his dad home would change everything for the better but his dad is suffering from a strange Underland illness and can barely walk round their tiny apartment, they are struggling to pay the bills and running out of food. It is early December and a light snow has fallen, Gregor takes his baby sister Boots to the park to go sledding, but whilst there she goes missing. Gregor finds a trail leading to the entrance to Underland and knows he must go back down and find his sister. Turns out there is another prophecy once more believed to be about him, he must save the Underlanders once more and fight off the monster that is the 'Bane'.<br />Being book 2 I feel like I know Gregor better and can understand his quirks and opinions and I continue to like him as a character and he is definitely developing into a promising hero. <br />This book is just as good, if not better than the first, the Quest seems filled with danger, but Gregor has his companions beside him. <br />I really liked teh bickering Fireflies they made me laugh, and little Temp - the Cockroach, strange to thing of a roach as sweet, but he really is endearing. Boots is growing up and developing more of a personality, often coming out with something seemingly random but actually helpful. Luxa is still ignoring all the rules and doing her own thing and I liek that about her.<br />There are new monsters and powers revealed in this book and it's just made me hungry for more.<br />There were moments in this book that literally had me gasping and gripping the pages. It ends with a bit of a mystery and I can't wait to get stuck into the next one and find out what has happened.<br />These books would be great for children who loved Harry Potter, Percy Jackson etc and are looking for something different.<br /></span>

<div id="review_684391231" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/684391231" />
    <a title="Jackie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1176067-jackie"><img alt="Jackie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1518141143p2/1176067.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/684391231?book_show_action=true">Aug 02, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jackie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jackie" href="/user/show/1176067-jackie">Jackie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1176067-jackie?shelf=2013-read">2013-read</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer684391231" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2397988397963462173">Okay, so after finishing Gregor the Overlander, I couldn’t wait to get to the second installment. I was left wondering at the aftereffects of Gregor’s return. How did he tell his mom about his adventures and how did she react? By the end of the first book I was just as worried as Gregor was about his return. <br/><br/>Unfortunately, home life hasn’t gotten any easier for Gregor and his family. Economically, they’re still struggling and emotionally they’re still dealing with the mysterious happenings of Un</span>
  <span id="freeText2397988397963462173" style="display:none">Okay, so after finishing Gregor the Overlander, I couldn’t wait to get to the second installment. I was left wondering at the aftereffects of Gregor’s return. How did he tell his mom about his adventures and how did she react? By the end of the first book I was just as worried as Gregor was about his return. <br /><br />Unfortunately, home life hasn’t gotten any easier for Gregor and his family. Economically, they’re still struggling and emotionally they’re still dealing with the mysterious happenings of Underland. Fortunately, despite the struggles Gregor still remains a thoughtful and responsible young man. I seriously want to hug this character! I love how he takes care of everyone, especially his little sisters. <br /><br />Despite Gregor’s return and the sealing of the laundry grate, the past adventures of Overland still hangs over the family. Gregor begins to find little roaches in the apartment and hear scratching inside the walls. He knows there is this ‘Prophecy of Bane’ hanging over his head, yet he hopes to never see Underland ever again. Fortunately for us readers that is not meant to be :) Yet again, Gregor finds himself in Underland after the roaches “kidnap” their princess Boots. In this adventure Gregor finds himself facing off the rats once again in an effort to save the kingdom by finding a white rat named the Bane. <br /><br />In this second book, we have some of the old characters who survived the trip like Ares, Luxa and her bat Aurora, Vikus and Solovet and even Ripred. We also meet some new ones. Luxa’s cousins from the non-royal side are rather interesting along with a new rat named Twitchtip. While Gregor’s adventure in this book was fun, I really found the secondary character stories more interesting. This second book has plenty of adventure and suspense, but it seemed like the focus was with dealing and overcoming the losses and emotions that occurred during the first adventure. I must say that Collins has a way of writing very relatable and emotional characters. Also, she is able to inject moral lessons easily into the story. Again, we have a story filled with the importance of family, friendship, love and working together in a cool adventurous story. Can’t wait to read the third book! <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="2397988397963462173" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_206792467" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/206792467" />
    <a title="Lucy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4089617-lucy"><img alt="Lucy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1358564977p2/4089617.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/206792467?book_show_action=true">Sep 09, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lucy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lucy" href="/user/show/4089617-lucy">Lucy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4089617-lucy?shelf=2011-reads">2011-reads</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer206792467" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3539424017261559997">An absolutely brilliant sequel to <i>Gregor the Overlander</i>. Anyone doubting Suzanne Collins' storytelling prowess should definitely give this series a try. I'd love to see Collins write a book for adults, since she's proven with this series and <i>The Hunger Games</i> that she's capable of writing fantastic, engaging stories for both children and young adults with ease.<br/><br/>I ordered the third book before I'd even finished this one and I'm very glad I did - there's a few loose ends at the end of this one that </span>
  <span id="freeText3539424017261559997" style="display:none">An absolutely brilliant sequel to <i>Gregor the Overlander</i>. Anyone doubting Suzanne Collins' storytelling prowess should definitely give this series a try. I'd love to see Collins write a book for adults, since she's proven with this series and <i>The Hunger Games</i> that she's capable of writing fantastic, engaging stories for both children and young adults with ease.<br /><br />I ordered the third book before I'd even finished this one and I'm very glad I did - there's a few loose ends at the end of this one that I think will be important in the next installment. I'm eagerly anticipating more from the Underland. I just hope the last two books are released in the U.K. sometime soon!</span>
  <a data-text-id="3539424017261559997" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Venus" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/39579143-venus"><img alt="Venus" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1479113987p2/39579143.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2067141893?book_show_action=true">Jul 21, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Venus" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Venus" href="/user/show/39579143-venus">Venus</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2067141893" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10917778895984540683">I love this series so freaking much. THG really cannot even compare in my opinion.<br/><br/><b>Pros</b><br/>- CHARACTERS. Wow, I love everyone so much. I could talk about Gregor for hours. He is so empathetic and courageous, but also completely fallible. He makes mistakes and has to correct his behavior/actions so many times throughout the book, and he's such a better character for it. Twitchtip completely stole my heart. What an incredible individual to include in this story. Technically part of the "wrong" side but</span>
  <span id="freeText10917778895984540683" style="display:none">I love this series so freaking much. THG really cannot even compare in my opinion.<br /><br /><b>Pros</b><br />- CHARACTERS. Wow, I love everyone so much. I could talk about Gregor for hours. He is so empathetic and courageous, but also completely fallible. He makes mistakes and has to correct his behavior/actions so many times throughout the book, and he's such a better character for it. Twitchtip completely stole my heart. What an incredible individual to include in this story. Technically part of the "wrong" side but so compelling and well-written. And I have to mention Mrs. Cormaci. She's barely even in the book, but I adore her.<br />- Prophecy. The last one was simply okay in my opinion, but this prophecy was so cleverly constructed. It convinces you fully of one thing, then you see the full picture and everything is, as Vikus and Nerissa say, "clear as water."<br />- Theme!!!!! I don't think I could ever get over how incredible it is that challenging ideas and difficult questions are presented in this book in understandable ways. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[The supposed villain of the story being just a baby was honestly a stroke of genius. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>Characters continue to struggle with their prejudices and the entire concept of "right vs. wrong" is called into question. <br /><br /><b>Cons</b><br />- I understand this is a middle-grade book, but the book felt a little short. Not exactly page-wise, but the journey could have had more space in the story to allow the reader to grow more familiar with certain characters. I liked Howard, for example, but I feel like I should know more about him.<br /><br /><b>Favorite Quote</b><br />“'We would have had no choice if the venom spread further, but Howard was able to suck it from the wounds,' said Mareth. <br /><br />'Ugh. Thanks, Howard,' Gregor said, gingerly flexing his fingers. Luxa scowled at him. 'What? He sucked venom from my arm! I can’t say thank you?'"<br /><br /><b>Final Thoughts</b><br />Why has everyone not read these books??? I'm rarely this excited about a series longer than a trilogy.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="10917778895984540683" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer12398313947998176723">In Gregor and the Prophecy of Bane by Suzanne Collins, Gregor hoped to never go back to the Underland and under his moms watchful eye he probably couldn't. When Boots suddenly disappears into one of the passage ways leading to the Underland Gregor has no choice, but to follow. In this follow up in the Underland Gregor faces the second of Bartholomew Sandwich's prophecies. I would suggest this book to anyone who liked the Hunger Games, Percy Jackson, or Harry Potter.</span>

          </span>

<div id="review_1950945335" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1950945335" />
    <a title="Caylynn" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/66237296-caylynn"><img alt="Caylynn" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1594527171p2/66237296.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1950945335?book_show_action=true">Mar 24, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Caylynn" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Caylynn" href="/user/show/66237296-caylynn">Caylynn</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1950945335" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9659689642283815163"><i>
  <blockquote>"But we need her! We need her to navigate the Labyrinth!"<br/><br/>"The bats will be sufficient," said Mareth. "And they can be trusted."<br/><br/>So, that was it. Now he understood. "It's because she's a rat. You're just going to sit here and watch her drown because she's a rat, right? If it were Howard or Andromeda or even Temp, you'd be down there, all right, but not for a rat!"</blockquote>
</i><br/>Honestly, this one was never really my <i>favorite</i> book out of the series. That honor will always belong to <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/385706.Gregor_and_the_Curse_of_the_Warmbloods__Underland_Chronicles___3_' title='Gregor and the Curse of the Warmbloods (Underland Chronicles, #3) by Suzanne Collins' rel='nofollow noopener'>Gregor and the Curse of the</a></span>
  <span id="freeText9659689642283815163" style="display:none"><i>
  <blockquote>"But we need her! We need her to navigate the Labyrinth!"<br /><br />"The bats will be sufficient," said Mareth. "And they can be trusted."<br /><br />So, that was it. Now he understood. "It's because she's a rat. You're just going to sit here and watch her drown because she's a rat, right? If it were Howard or Andromeda or even Temp, you'd be down there, all right, but not for a rat!"</blockquote>
</i><br />Honestly, this one was never really my <i>favorite</i> book out of the series. That honor will always belong to <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/385706.Gregor_and_the_Curse_of_the_Warmbloods__Underland_Chronicles___3_" title="Gregor and the Curse of the Warmbloods (Underland Chronicles, #3) by Suzanne Collins" rel="nofollow noopener">Gregor and the Curse of the Warmbloods</a>. Aside from the fact that this book introduces the "big bad"-like, Voldemort big bad, guys- of the series, it always seemed to me that this was more of a filler book than anything. <br /><br />Does that mean I <i>didn't</i> like it? HELL NO. I still <i>
  <b>loved</b>
</i> it. It's just like my fourth favorite out of the five books. I physically CAN'T dislike any of these books, because they're all amazing in their own ways. This one was just a little more...stagnant than the others. The plot and the quest in this one could've really been melded into one of the other books or made much shorter. But then again, we got a more in depth look at some of the main characters that wouldn't have been as beneficial had it been mushed into another book and skimmed over. So it's iffy as to whether making this quest its own book was avoidable or not. <br /><br />In <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/385742.Gregor_and_the_Prophecy_of_Bane__Underland_Chronicles___2_" title="Gregor and the Prophecy of Bane (Underland Chronicles, #2) by Suzanne Collins" rel="nofollow noopener">Gregor and the Prophecy of Bane</a>, we see a <i>lot</i> of character development in Gregor, Ares, Mareth and his bat, Luxa, and even the new guy Howard, whom I love with all of my heart <s>and I was dead set on marrying him when I read this for the first time oh so many years ago, don't tell anyone.</s> We get to see Gregor and Ares grow stronger over their new human/flier bond for life, even though at the beginning of the book they were arguing pretty hard. We get a little more insight into mysterious Queen Luxa, and see how she's dealing with the aftermath of <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Henry's betrayal and fall to his death <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>.<br /><br />But, best of all, we are introduced to the beloved fan fav Howard of Fount, Luxa's cousin on her mother's side and the nicest out of his four other siblings by FAR. Seriously, his second oldest sibling is a real bitch to Luxa. At first you really dislike him, because Luxa describes him as horrid and Gregor/the readers automatically believe her and form prejudice against him and his siblings because that's the way Collins wrote it, you clever author, you. But then, once Gregor gets to know him (pretty much <i>right</i> away) he learns that Howard is actually a really nice guy and Luxa may have been wrong about him. Just, the way Suzanne Collins is able to easily write about subliminal thoughts/beliefs and personal stereotypes once they've been suggested to you is fucking <i>
  <b>brilliant</b>
</i> and I'm always amazed. Like, LOOK AT THIS MISCONCEPTION:<br /><i>
  <blockquote> [Luxa is accusing Howard of tormenting their other cousin Nerissa] "At the festival. When you set that lizard on her!" said Luxa.<br /><br />"Set it? I did not set it! That was a rare color changer, and I thought it would amuse her to see it!"<br /><br />"But Henry said he saw you-" began Luxa.<br /><br />"Henry said? <b>Henry</b> said? I cannot believe that even now you do not question things that Henry said! Is he the one who told you I was after your crown?" Howard's voice rose in frustration. "HENRY said!"</blockquote>
</i><br />The power of suggested conception, everybody. It's similar to when a girl is walking home alone (whether during the day or night, you choose) and notices that a guy is walking behind her as well. It could be that he IS just walking in the same direction, because she's on a college campus and they could both be heading to the same class. But, no matter what, that girl is most likely going to think that the guy is following her and has ill intentions towards her, because that's just what we as females have learned to think like. I just, ugh, it hits hard the way Collins writes this way for a lot of her characters. <br /><br />This sequel was definitely character centric, which I love. I just wish the plot was as thick though. It would probably be bumped way up the list if that was so. Oh well, I still immensely enjoy it every time I reread it, so I can't complain! And it still deals with the overlying issues of "racism" (I say this in quotes because it's more like "speciesism" but I don't know if that's what I'm going for here), prejudice, war, violence, death, etc. <br /><br />On to the next one, AKA my FAVORITE!</span>
  <a data-text-id="9659689642283815163" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_464119457" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/464119457" />
    <a title="Mike" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/12248943-mike"><img alt="Mike" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1499990463p2/12248943.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/464119457?book_show_action=true">Nov 26, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mike" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mike" href="/user/show/12248943-mike">Mike</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12248943-mike?shelf=good-middle-grade">good-middle-grade</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12248943-mike?shelf=thrillers">thrillers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12248943-mike?shelf=high-fantasy">high-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12248943-mike?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12248943-mike?shelf=action">action</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12248943-mike?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12248943-mike?shelf=third-person">third-person</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12248943-mike?shelf=good-books-have-good-covers">good-books-have-good-covers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12248943-mike?shelf=magic">magic</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer464119457" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6841379079868348322">Here we are, at book two in the Underland Chronicles, Suzanne Collin's MG series published before <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2767052.The_Hunger_Games__The_Hunger_Games__1_' title='The Hunger Games (The Hunger Games #1) by Suzanne Collins' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Hunger Games</a>. General consensus seems to be that The Hunger Games was far better, and while I agree that this wasn't as good, it's still certainly a worthwhile read, underrated among Suzanne Collins fans.<br/><br/>The biggest reason being that Collins's wonderful plotting skill is on display once again. While the adventures occasionally felt episodic, the pacing was fast and consistent, an important featu</span>
  <span id="freeText6841379079868348322" style="display:none">Here we are, at book two in the Underland Chronicles, Suzanne Collin's MG series published before <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2767052.The_Hunger_Games__The_Hunger_Games__1_" title="The Hunger Games (The Hunger Games #1) by Suzanne Collins" rel="nofollow noopener">The Hunger Games</a>. General consensus seems to be that The Hunger Games was far better, and while I agree that this wasn't as good, it's still certainly a worthwhile read, underrated among Suzanne Collins fans.<br /><br />The biggest reason being that Collins's wonderful plotting skill is on display once again. While the adventures occasionally felt episodic, the pacing was fast and consistent, an important feature of MG fantasy. It's also genuinely unpredictable, which is pretty rare for MG, since kids are so bad at predicting things. But the plot here is constantly surprising, with a great prophecy twist (and another twist that I'd call one of the best I've ever seen), a plot that manages to be simple but still interesting.<br /><br />I suppose it works so well for the same reason The Hunger Games worked so well: Gregor is a nice hero to see the Underland from. He could be a bit annoying at times, but his characterization remained strong, and I can see him growing as the series goes along. The side characters aren't quite as consistent. Some of them were just as interesting as Gregor - of particular note is Ares, whose banishment is realistically handled, which makes him sympathetic. But some of the other characters were... not so interesting, to say the least. Like the fireflies that we meet, for example - their only purpose seemed to be to annoy everyone, the audience included.<br /><br />As with the first book, the writing was pretty good, except for the fact that Collins tries to be voicey with the third person, which I've always found annoying and never found effective. It's not constant, and Gregor's voice doesn't exactly jump out at you, but it still feels out of place in the third-person narration. But other than that, Collins's prose is strong and well-written. It won't blow you off your feet, but it carries the story quite well, and it's mostly effective.<br /><br />I'm finding that I have the same issues and merits that I had with the first book, although I'd say that I like this one better. I suspect that the entire series will be enjoyable as this one, which is why I'm going to go ahead and recommend reading, even after just two books. It's no Hunger Games, but it's well-written and well-plotted. That's more than I can say about a lot of other books.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6841379079868348322" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1905876561?book_show_action=true">Feb 07, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Eric N." class="user" itemprop="url" name="Eric N." href="/user/show/64582226-eric-n">Eric N.</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1905876561" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1799562713263910068">It has been a couple months since Gregor has been in the Underland but when Boots is kidnapped by the Crawlers he must go back. When he arrives in Regalia he soon reads the Prophecy of Bane and learns that the Gnawers are trying to kill Boots and he has to kill "The Bane". In order to find the Bane he sails across the waterway with Luxa, Aurora, Mareth, Andromeda, Ares, Boots, Temp, Twitchtip, Photos Glow-Glow, Zap, Howard, and Pandora. Along the way they run into problems that only makes things</span>
  <span id="freeText1799562713263910068" style="display:none">It has been a couple months since Gregor has been in the Underland but when Boots is kidnapped by the Crawlers he must go back. When he arrives in Regalia he soon reads the Prophecy of Bane and learns that the Gnawers are trying to kill Boots and he has to kill "The Bane". In order to find the Bane he sails across the waterway with Luxa, Aurora, Mareth, Andromeda, Ares, Boots, Temp, Twitchtip, Photos Glow-Glow, Zap, Howard, and Pandora. Along the way they run into problems that only makes things worse, some of the problems are a giant squid, a whirlpool, and an island with flesh-eating mites.Those are not the last of their problems however, more await them in the Labyrinth. I loved the book I loved the plot and the cliffhanger at the end. I also enjoyed the reveal of the meaning of the Prophecy of Bane. One thing that I wish there was more of was a little bit more action, but all in all in was an amazing book. If you enjoyed this book another series that you may enjoy is the Percy Jackson series.</span>

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1875312252?book_show_action=true">Feb 20, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nora Eliana | Papertea &amp; Bookflowers" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nora Eliana | Papertea &amp; Bookflowers" href="/user/show/32866883-nora-eliana-papertea-bookflowers">Nora Eliana | Papertea &amp; Bookflowers</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Nora Eliana | Papertea &amp; Bookflowers by: </span>
      Annika 
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32866883-nora-eliana-papertea-bookflowers?shelf=series">series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32866883-nora-eliana-papertea-bookflowers?shelf=read-in-2017">read-in-2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32866883-nora-eliana-papertea-bookflowers?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32866883-nora-eliana-papertea-bookflowers?shelf=recommended-to-me">recommended-to-me</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32866883-nora-eliana-papertea-bookflowers?shelf=children-books">children-books</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1875312252" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2423762961886388419"><i> Actual Rating: 4.5 stars </i><br/><br/>I <i> love </i> this series! I do! But I hate the audiobook. Especially, well mostly that, the way the narrator speaks Boots. I couldn't stand it and had to go and buy the book to be able to finish it. <br/><br/>For a time I thought middle grade just isn’t for me. That I can’t get into the stories anymore and I was kinda sad about it. And I was afraid to reread some of my favorites because of that. I didn’t want to taint the memories. <br/>But I absolutely love this series! And there is noth</span>
  <span id="freeText2423762961886388419" style="display:none"><i> Actual Rating: 4.5 stars </i><br /><br />I <i> love </i> this series! I do! But I hate the audiobook. Especially, well mostly that, the way the narrator speaks Boots. I couldn't stand it and had to go and buy the book to be able to finish it. <br /><br />For a time I thought middle grade just isn’t for me. That I can’t get into the stories anymore and I was kinda sad about it. And I was afraid to reread some of my favorites because of that. I didn’t want to taint the memories. <br />But I absolutely love this series! And there is nothing nostalgic about it since I haven’t read it when <br />I was younger. So thank you for restoring my love for middle-grade fiction!<br /><br />Suzanne Collins manages to write captivating, young and fun while tackling difficult topics and not shying away from tragic or bad things happening. Nothing is completely black and white, but complex. And I loved how the prophecy unfolded. <br /><br />All the characters felt very realistic to me - and their development after the events in the first book too - and I love Boots to pieces! <br />And how Gregor cares for her.<br /><br />Also, his and Ares relationship was awesome and so realistic! I can’t say much about it other than that I absolutely adore this series and can’t wait to continue. It’s seriously underrated! </span>
  <a data-text-id="2423762961886388419" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer16114775312950862233">The Prophecy of Bane predicted the return of Gregor the overlander to the underland world to take the light of the Bane and return the light to Regalia. That's the one-sentence layout of the book.<br/>But to try and describe the amount of emotions this book contains, it'd be challenging to try to describe it.<br/>In this book, Collins made an improvement.   <span id="freeText16114775312950862233" style="display:none">The Prophecy of Bane predicted the return of Gregor the overlander to the underland world to take the light of the Bane and return the light to Regalia. That's the one-sentence layout of the book.<br />But to try and describe the amount of emotions this book contains, it'd be challenging to try to describe it.<br />In this book, Collins made an improvement. She took more care of the psychological profiling of the main characters and some of the side characters.<br />Boots is still my favorite character.<br />This book's ending feels like an abrupt stop, but there're three more books in this series. So, lets just wait and see what happens next.</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2678333732" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13046449128376810920">This story expanded so much from the first one. We get another fascinating prophecy to try and unfold as well as many new characters. Most of this novel takes place on the waterways in underland. I found this novel to take a much darker tone than the first one did and I personally loved it. I loved all of the characters so much and can’t wait to see how else they will grow. This story focused on the prophecy of Bane who is a white rat that Gregor is to kill. I’m loving this series so far and can</span>
  <span id="freeText13046449128376810920" style="display:none">This story expanded so much from the first one. We get another fascinating prophecy to try and unfold as well as many new characters. Most of this novel takes place on the waterways in underland. I found this novel to take a much darker tone than the first one did and I personally loved it. I loved all of the characters so much and can’t wait to see how else they will grow. This story focused on the prophecy of Bane who is a white rat that Gregor is to kill. I’m loving this series so far and can’t wait to continue this re read. </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('Q46XO0LSQhhE3imAxsQi9gFFQ3uM6KMmIRg/whKvO9vBDV1EFCIHeU2CZFvhT2Lpse1Q8eb55V7bFmY+0DQWlQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('rWRXOGIKk5DOftAYQWR00QkJNGFJAZA5QtwHAQw0r5Yv551HNPrW8ccincNm7zTOuaEn6yMQ1kG40l79zq+C2A==')})
  }

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer9891529547260816109"><i>Librarian Note: There is more than one author in the Goodreads database with this name.</i><br/><br/>Since 1991, Suzanne Collins has been busy writing for children’s television. She has worked on the staffs of several Nickelodeon shows, including the Emmy-nominated hit Clarissa Explains it All and The Mystery Files of Shelby Woo. For preschool viewers, she penned multiple stories for the Emmy-nominated Little B</span>
  <span id="freeText9891529547260816109" style="display:none"><i>Librarian Note: There is more than one author in the Goodreads database with this name.</i><br /><br />Since 1991, Suzanne Collins has been busy writing for children’s television. She has worked on the staffs of several Nickelodeon shows, including the Emmy-nominated hit Clarissa Explains it All and The Mystery Files of Shelby Woo. For preschool viewers, she penned multiple stories for the Emmy-nominated Little Bear and Oswald. She also co-wrote the critically acclaimed Rankin/Bass Christmas special, Santa, Baby! Most recently she was the Head Writer for Scholastic Entertainment’s Clifford’s Puppy Days.<br /><br />While working on a Kids WB show called Generation O! she met children’s author James Proimos, who talked her into giving children’s books a try.<br /><br />Thinking one day about Alice in Wonderland, she was struck by how pastoral the setting must seem to kids who, like her own, lived in urban surroundings. In New York City, you’re much more likely to fall down a manhole than a rabbit hole and, if you do, you’re not going to find a tea party. What you might find...? Well, that’s the story of Gregor the Overlander, the first book in her five-part series, The Underland Chronicles. Suzanne also has a rhyming picture book illustrated by Mike Lester entitled When Charlie McButton Lost Power.<br /><br />She currently lives in Connecticut with her family and a pair of feral kittens they adopted from their backyard.<br /><br />The books she is most successful for in teenage eyes are The Hunger Games, Catching Fire and Mockingjay. These books have won several awards, including the GA Peach Award. </span>
